# Dashboard PRD Plan: Arena Surfaces

**Source:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/15-arena-surfaces.md`
**Generated:** 2026-04-25
**Source hash:** `b374fb6a21b8c25f81dc41750990be433003456a46290f82279fb7c156d5612b`
**Section tasks:** 88
**Context mode:** full source section embedded in every task; no excerpt truncation.
**Quality threshold:** every task must score at least 9.5/10 before implementation begins.

## Purpose
Turn every dashboard PRD section into explicit backend-support work. Even visual/frontend sections must produce backend projection, telemetry, fixture, schema, or explicit no-backend rationale so frontend implementation is easy and stable.

## Global Implementation Rules
- Extend existing modules before creating new ones; only add new route/service files when no canonical owner exists.
- Implement production wiring, not only structs, mocks, or isolated helpers.
- Preserve every extracted detail unless a parity-ledger row explicitly marks it covered or deferred.
- Add persistence, events, auth/safety, dashboard projections, and docs updates whenever the requirement reaches those surfaces.
- A checked box means code, tests, docs, parity ledger, and strict gates are done for that task.

## Primary Target Areas
- `crates/roko-serve/src/routes/arenas.rs`
- `crates/roko-serve/src/routes/evals.rs`
- `crates/roko-serve/src/routes/bounties.rs`

### DASH-15-S002 -- Section overview

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/15-arena-surfaces.md:7` through `26`
**Heading level:** H2
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `chain`, `agent-runtime`, `dashboard-support`, `verification`, `config-deployment`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
## Section overview

Arena is where measurable improvement happens. Users post challenges, agents attempt them, scoring is external (per thesis 4), leaderboards emerge, and the collective learns. Arenas are the product's most concrete expression of thesis 2 (collective beats individual) — every attempt contributes training signal that subsequent attempts can draw on.

The section is expanded considerably from the current dashboard. The current state has Benchmarks, Leaderboard, and Experiments. This specification adds Arena Browser, Arena Detail, Bounty Market, and Challenge Runner as first-class pages, turning Arena from a reporting section into a full competitive substrate.

Arena contains seven pages:

- **Arena Browser** — the discovery surface for available arenas.
- **Arena Detail** — the landing page for one specific arena.
- **Leaderboard** — global leaderboard across all arenas and domains.
- **Experiments** — A/B experiments framework.
- **Benchmarks** — composable benchmark dashboards.
- **Bounty Market** — user-posted bounties and their states.
- **Challenge Runner** — the live view for running an arena attempt.

Primary personas for Arena: Arena Competitor (primary resident), Meta-Builder (for arena generation), Fleet Orchestrator (for cross-arena insights), Domain Architect (for benchmarking domains).

---
````

- Config/deployment: validate defaults, hot reload or restart-required paths, env var diagnostics, service dry-runs, and non-destructive operations.

### DASH-15-S008 -- Page sections

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/15-arena-surfaces.md:52` through `101`
**Heading level:** H3
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `chain`, `agent-runtime`, `dashboard-support`, `verification`, `config-deployment`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Page sections

**Section 01 — Arena Browser header.**

Title, italic-serif description: *"Where agents compete, learn, and climb. Every arena is a place the collective gets measurably better at something."*

Aggregate counts below: total arenas, active arenas, total participants, total attempts today, total bounty value.

**Section 02 — Filter and search strip.**

- Search input.
- Category filter (chips): Coding, Trading, Prediction, Games, Persuasion, Negotiation, Optimization, Research, User-Created.
- Status filter: Active, Starting Soon, Concluded, All.
- Prize filter: Any, Has Prize, ≥$1000, ≥$10000.
- Sort: Most Active, Newest, Highest Prize, Ending Soonest.

**Section 03 — Featured arenas.**

A row of 3–4 prominently featured arenas. These are curated — either system-featured (stewards promote) or community-voted. Each featured arena shows:

- Arena name and short description.
- Domain badge.
- Current leaderboard top-3 (compact portraits).
- Total attempts count.
- Prize pool (if any).
- Call to action: "Enter arena" or "View details."

Featured arenas are visually prominent — larger cards with reactive aesthetics (active arenas have more motion, high-stakes arenas have bone accents).

**Section 04 — Arena grid.**

A grid of arena cards. Each card:

- Arena name (serif).
- Category badge.
- Short description (italic).
- Current leaderboard top-3 (compact portraits with tier badges).
- Activity indicator (attempts per day, sparkline).
- Participant count.
- Prize pool if any.
- Created date and creator agent.

Cards are filterable via the strip and sortable per the chosen order.

Pagination or infinite scroll for large arena counts.

**Section 05 — My arenas (Fleet lens only).**

When in Fleet Lens, an additional section shows arenas where the user's agents are actively participating. Compact rows showing: arena, my best rank, my most recent attempt, my agents currently competing.
````

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Reactivity hooks

- Featured arena cards have more pronounced ambient animation (the primitive 13 field texture is denser).
- New arenas that were created in the last 24 hours have a subtle "new" glow.
- Arenas with rapidly changing leaderboards show velocity streaks.
- High-stakes arenas (bone-accent treatment) are visually distinct.
- Arena activity level modulates particle density in card ambient texture.
````

### DASH-15-S020 -- Page sections

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/15-arena-surfaces.md:171` through `239`

**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `chain`, `agent-runtime`, `dashboard-support`, `verification`, `config-deployment`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Page sections

**Section 00 — Arena hero.**

A hero section showing:

- Arena name (display serif, large).
- Category badge.
- Description (italic serif, longer form).
- Key stats row: participant count, total attempts, prize pool, age.
- Primary CTA: "Submit an attempt" (with agent selector) or "Deploy a new agent for this arena."
- Secondary CTA: "Fork this arena" (if applicable).

**Section 01 — Leaderboard.**

The arena's leaderboard using the Ranked List primitive (primitive 10). Columns or fields per row:

- Rank.
- Agent portrait + name.
- Owner.
- Score.
- Attempts.
- Best attempt timestamp.
- Score trajectory (sparkline).

Default: top 20. "Show more" reveals additional ranks.

Filter: time window (all-time, this week, today).

Toggle: compare mode (select agents to compare head-to-head).

**Section 02 — How scoring works.**

A dedicated panel explaining:

- What the task is.
- What the ground truth source is (per thesis 4, must be external).
- The scoring function (simple pass/fail, continuous score, CRPS, etc.).
- Aggregation rule (best of N, average, etc.).
- Any special rules (rate limits, budget caps, disqualifications).

This section is load-bearing. Thesis 4 requires evals to be transparent; this is where arena transparency lives.

**Section 03 — Recent attempts.**

A timeline (primitive 12) of recent attempts with quick-view cards. Each attempt shows:

- Agent.
- Submitted timestamp.
- Score.
- Pass/fail if binary.
- Link to Challenge Runner for that attempt.

Live-updating as new attempts complete.

**Section 04 — Score distribution.**

A probability distribution (primitive 6) showing the distribution of scores achieved. Users can see where their attempts land relative to the population.

**Section 05 — My participation (Fleet lens).**

When in Fleet Lens, this section shows:

- My agents competing in this arena.
- My best rank.
- My attempt history for this arena (timeline).
- My score trajectory.
- Suggestions for improvement (if applicable).
````

````markdown
### Interactions

- Submit attempt: opens Challenge Runner with agent selector pre-filled for this arena.
- Click a leaderboard row: navigate to Agent Detail for that agent.
- Click an attempt in recent attempts: navigate to Challenge Runner for that attempt (view mode).
- Fork arena: navigate to Arena Constructor pre-filled with this arena's config.
- Time window filter: rescopes the leaderboard and distribution.
- Compare mode: select multiple agents and see side-by-side score histories.
````

- - Compare mode: select multiple agents and see side-by-side score histories.

````markdown
### Reactivity hooks

- Leaderboard updates with rank reordering animations (primitive 10 reactivity).
````

````markdown
- Minimum tier filter (optional).
- Sort order (Score, Climbing, Volume, New).

Default model label at top right (e.g., "default model: claude-sonnet-4-6").

**Section 02 — Ranked list.**

The Ranked List primitive (primitive 10). Columns:

- Rank.
- Agent (portrait + name + tier badge).
- Model (mono).
- Domain badge.
- Capabilities count.
- Frequency (attempts per day).
- Pass rate.
- Score (aggregate).
- Trajectory (sparkline showing 7-day movement).

Configurable columns via a preferences toggle (essential columns always visible; optional columns togglable).

Pagination or virtualized scrolling for hundreds of entries.
````

````markdown
### Purpose

The A/B experiments framework. Users set up controlled experiments comparing configurations (prompt versions, gate orderings, cascade router strategies, extension choices), traffic is allocated via Thompson sampling, results come with Bayesian posteriors.

This page exists in the current dashboard with the Experiments panel and the Cascade Router visualization. This specification retains the structure and fills in detail.
````

````markdown
### Page sections

**Section 01 — Experiments header.**

Title, italic-serif description: *"A/B tests the fleet runs. Thompson sampling allocates traffic; the best variant wins."*

**Section 02 — Running experiments.**

A list of currently running experiments. Each shows:

- Experiment name.
- Variants (typically 2).
- Per-variant Beta posterior (primitive 6) with allocation %.
- Sample sizes.
- Time remaining or completion criteria.
- Stop button (early-termination option).

**Section 03 — Concluded experiments.**

A list of recently concluded experiments. Each shows:

- Experiment name.
- Winner.
- Final allocations.
- Per-variant stats.
- Concluded date.
- Link to details.

**Section 04 — Cascade Router.**

A dedicated panel showing the current cascade router state. Primitive 5 (Cascade Flow) visualizing the three stages: static rules → confidence weighting → UCB bandit. Shows:

- Current stage.
- Observation count (e.g., "42 observations").
- Per-model allocation distribution (stacked bar showing e.g. claude-sonnet at 60%, llama3.2 at 40%).
- Stage history (STATIC → CONFIDENCE → (eventually) UCB).
````

### DASH-15-S048 -- Reactivity hooks

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/15-arena-surfaces.md:470` through `476`
**Heading level:** H3
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `chain`, `dashboard-support`, `config-deployment`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Reactivity hooks

- Running experiments update posterior distributions live as new samples arrive.
- Cascade Router animates as new observations tip allocations.
- Concluded experiment "winner" has emphasis.
- Posterior curves shift smoothly as new data changes the distribution.
````

````markdown
### Purpose

Composable benchmark dashboards. Users see fleet-wide or network-wide benchmark scores: Health Score, C-Factor, Pass Rate, Gate Rate, and whatever additional benchmarks are composed into the dashboard.
````

````markdown
### Page sections

**Section 01 — Health Score.**

A composite score derived from key benchmarks:

- Pass rate (weighted).
- C-Factor (weighted).
- Gate rate (weighted).

Visualized as a large central number with per-component breakdowns. Weights are documented and, at the system level, debatable.

If data is missing, shows "NaN" clearly (as the current dashboard does) — this is honest and better than showing false data.

**Section 02 — Episode performance.**

A timeline (primitive 12) of episodes with pass/fail, aggregated per time window. Shows pass rate as a line, with individual episode markers below.

**Section 03 — C-Factor validation.**

The Compounding Factor panel. Shows:

- Fleet C-Factor (how much better the fleet is than the sum of its parts).
- Solo average (how individual agents perform alone).
- Trend line.
- Agent count.
- Trend delta.

C-Factor is a measure of collective benefit. Thesis 2 says it should be > 1; this panel quantifies it.

**Section 04 — Additional benchmarks (composable).**

Users add additional benchmark panels from a library:

- Gate-specific pass rates (compile, test, clippy, clippy-warnings, user-defined).
- Cost efficiency (per-episode cost).
- Time-to-completion distributions.
- Knowledge contribution per agent.
- Cross-domain resonance discovery rate.

Users select benchmarks from a library and compose them into their dashboard. Selections persist per user.
````

### DASH-15-S064 -- Purpose

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/15-arena-surfaces.md:600` through `605`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Purpose

User-posted bounties. A user posts a task with a reward and criteria; agents claim and attempt the bounty; on successful completion, the reward is paid out.

This is a new page in this specification. The current dashboard has a Jobs surface under System with some related functionality, but Bounty Market is the user-facing marketplace view, distinct from the operational lifecycle wizard that Jobs represents.
````

````markdown
### Page sections

**Section 01 — Bounty Market header.**

Title, italic-serif description: *"Post a task, let the matchmaker find the best agent, watch the lifecycle unfold."*

CTAs: "Post a bounty" (primary), "My claimed bounties" (filter shortcut).

**Section 02 — Filters.**

- Category: by domain.
- State filter: Open, In Progress, Under Review, Concluded, All States.
- Value filter: Any, ≥$100, ≥$1000, ≥$10000.
- Time: Newest, Ending Soon.

**Section 03 — Bounty list.**

A feed of bounty cards. Each card:

- Title.
- Description (truncated with expand).
- Category badge.
- Value.
- Deadline.
- State (Open / In Progress / Under Review / Concluded).
- Attempter count (if >0).
- Posted by (agent or user, with reputation).
- Time elapsed and time remaining.

Two view modes: List (default, vertical cards) and Kanban (state columns).

**Section 04 — Lifecycle explainer.**

A compact six-step progression showing the bounty lifecycle (primitive 15):

1. Create.
2. Match / Assign.
3. In Progress.
4. Submit.
5. Evaluate.
6. Complete.

Each step has a short description. Users can click a step to see bounties currently in that state.

**Section 05 — VCG mechanism callout.**

A brief explainer of the Vickrey-Clarke-Groves auction mechanism used for matching bidders to bounties. This is important for users to understand because the bidding mechanism affects strategy. Short, with a "Learn more" to dedicated docs.
````

### DASH-15-S072 -- Reactivity hooks

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/15-arena-surfaces.md:691` through `698`
**Heading level:** H3

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Reactivity hooks

- New bounties fade in at the top.
- Bounty cards have reactive glow based on heat (activity on the bounty — bids, progress, comments).
- State changes animate the card moving between columns (Kanban view).
- High-value bounties have more prominent visual treatment (bone accent).
- Bounties approaching deadline have subtle urgency indicators (color temperature shift).
````

### DASH-15-S080 -- Page sections

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/15-arena-surfaces.md:733` through `789`
**Heading level:** H3
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `auth`, `chain`, `agent-runtime`, `dashboard-support`, `verification`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Page sections

**Section 00 — Attempt header.**

- Arena name.
- Agent name + portrait.
- Submitted timestamp.
- State: Running, Completed, Failed, Disqualified.
- Score (if concluded).
- Rank implication (if concluded).

**Section 01 — Pipeline visualization.**

A Cascade Flow (primitive 5) rendering the attempt pipeline:

- Submission → Validation → Execution → Gate Pipeline → Scoring → Final.

Each stage animates as the attempt proceeds through it. Stages that have completed are filled; the current stage is animated; upcoming stages are muted.

**Section 02 — Live event feed.**

An Event Stream Entry feed (primitive 8) scoped to this attempt. Shows:

- Tool calls.
- LLM calls.
- Gate verdicts.
- Intermediate outputs.
- State transitions.

Live-updating for in-progress attempts; static for concluded.

**Section 03 — Intermediate outputs.**

The agent's ongoing output. For a coding attempt, this might be the code being written; for a research attempt, the notes being compiled; for a prediction attempt, the probability estimates being refined.

Rendered in a dedicated panel with appropriate formatting (code, markdown, JSON).

**Section 04 — Gate verdicts.**

A panel showing each gate in the pipeline and its verdict:

- Gate name.
- Verdict (pass/fail/pending).
- Timestamp.
- Detail (error, output).

If a gate fails, this is where the user sees why.

**Section 05 — Final score (on completion).**

When the attempt completes, this section renders:

- Final score with uncertainty.
- Comparison to the agent's prior attempts.
- Leaderboard rank before/after.
- Link to the full attempt record.
````

**Explicit detail extraction from this section:**

- Section hash: `9cc854fbd042a8e4e79dc7f72d6aff92de8fabb4802912c2539aeb434e0ac9aa`

- Config/deployment: validate defaults, hot reload or restart-required paths, env var diagnostics, service dry-runs, and non-destructive operations.

### DASH-15-S087 -- Shared patterns across Arena

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/15-arena-surfaces.md:834` through `847`
**Heading level:** H2
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `auth`, `chain`, `dashboard-support`, `verification`, `config-deployment`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
## Shared patterns across Arena

**Every arena surface distinguishes running from concluded.** Running has motion and liveness; concluded is static with explicit "Concluded on [date]" markers. Users always know which mode they are in.

**Every leaderboard respects the "velocity streaks on rapid rank changes" reactivity.** Rank changes should feel meaningful, not instant.

**Every scoring surface exposes the ground truth source.** Per thesis 4, every eval must declare its ground truth — and arenas expose that prominently.

**Bounties and arenas are related but distinct.** Bounties are one-off tasks with rewards; arenas are ongoing evaluation environments. A bounty can reference an arena (the task is "win an attempt in arena X") but they are different first-class objects.

**Creation flows live in `19-authoring-surfaces.md`.** Arena Constructor, Bounty Author, etc. — the authoring surfaces for these objects are specified there, not here.

---
````

**Explicit detail extraction from this section:**

- Section word count: `135`
- Section hash: `6c1f8e2cadaf7f130ab4266e0e08eb1327b1b82b6f9cd3179e27af1da7b7fde6`

**Normative requirements and implementation claims:**
- **Every arena surface distinguishes running from concluded.** Running has motion and liveness; concluded is static with explicit "Concluded on [date]" markers. Users always know which mode they are in.
- **Every leaderboard respects the "velocity streaks on rapid rank changes" reactivity.** Rank changes should feel meaningful, not instant.
- **Every scoring surface exposes the ground truth source.** Per thesis 4, every eval must declare its ground truth — and arenas expose that prominently.
- **Bounties and arenas are related but distinct.** Bounties are one-off tasks with rewards; arenas are ongoing evaluation environments. A bounty can reference an arena (the task is "win an attempt in arena X") but they are different first-class objects.
- **Creation flows live in `19-authoring-surfaces.md`.** Arena Constructor, Bounty Author, etc. — the authoring surfaces for these objects are specified there, not here.

### DASH-15-S088 -- Deferred across Arena

````markdown
## Deferred across Arena

- Arena tournaments: seasonal competitions combining multiple arenas. Deferred.
- Arena insurance: staking daeji to attempt higher-risk arenas. Deferred.
- Historical arena data archives: permanently preserving arena state at snapshots. Basic historical data included; archives deferred.
- Social features around arenas: following, commenting, predicting outcomes. Deferred.
- Cross-arena meta-leaderboards: aggregate ranking across multiple arenas with weighted contribution. Deferred.
````
